Core Defense Mechanism: The 50/50 Principle (Logical Restructuring)"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"This is the most subversive financial rule in this chapter: "},{"type":"text","text":"apart from daily living expenses, use 50% of the surplus to pay off debt, and the remaining 50% is strictly deposited into a \"goose account.\"","bold":true}]},{"type":"ul","children":[{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Wealth consciousness \"firewall\"","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":": If you use all your money to pay off debt, your account will still be at zero the day you pay it off. A person who doesn't spend is just \"someone who spends less\"; a person who saves is \"someone who is accumulating wealth.\" The former's result is that there happens to be a balance in the account; the latter's result is that you are executing a financial plan. The best way to turn \"natural surplus\" into \"conscious saving\" is to physically separate savings and daily expenses into different accounts."}]},{"type":"h3","children":[{"type":"text","text":"3. Retention of Power: The Psychological Tactic of Cash Reserves"}]},{"type":"ul","children":[{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Meaning of reserve funds","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":": No matter how heavy the debt, a non-negotiable cash reserve (e.g., 25,000 euros) must be kept in a safe."}]}]}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"80% of the pressure on heavily indebted individuals does not come from the total debt, but from having no money to cover tomorrow's expenses. Not linked to any payments, treated as non-existent in daily life."}]}]},{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"\"Treat it as non-existent\": This money is deposited and then untouched, neither entering nor leaving. Its purpose is not to grow in value, but to provide a buffer for you to restart and calmly think of solutions in the worst-case scenario."}]}]},{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Do not use even in bankruptcy: The book emphasizes that this reserve fund should only be used in case of bankruptcy or legal declaration. Sympathy will trap you in a victim mentality. Winners should earn respect, and respect comes from taking 100% responsibility for your debts, blaming no one."}]}]}]},{"type":"h3","children":[{"type":"text","text":"5. Bankruptcy: When There's No Other Choice"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"If bankruptcy is inevitable, \"11:55\" is better than \"12:00.\" The "},{"type":"text","text":"earlier","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":" you make the decision, the more resources you retain and the more room you have to restart."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Bankruptcy decisions must be made in consultation with an experienced bankruptcy attorney. Sometimes, continuing to struggle costs more than starting over—\"pushing an old car out of deep mud can be much harder than buying a new one.\""}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Bankruptcy may mean giving up a business into which you've poured a lot of time, energy, and money. This requires distinguishing between optimism and reality—if something has been slowly getting worse for a long time, it won't suddenly get better without change."}]},{"type":"h3","children":[{"type":"text","text":"6. Practical Guide to Eliminating Debt"}]},{"type":"ol","children":[{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Belief Liquidation","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":": Identify old beliefs that led to your debt (e.g., \"I deserve this luxury item\") and break them."}]}]},{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Physical Isolation","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":": Cut up all credit cards, severing the source of consumer debt."}]}]},{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Goal Replacement","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":": Don't fight not to lose (pay off debt), fight to win (get rich). Debt is a \"toxic situation\"; you need to extract the medicine called \"growth\" from it."}]}]}]},{"type":"hr","children":[{"type":"text","text":""}]},{"type":"h2","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Chapter 7 How to Increase Your Income"}]},{"type":"h3","children":[{"type":"text","text":"1. A Fundamental Premise: Your Income is What You Deserve"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"All content in this chapter is built on an uncomfortable premise: "},{"type":"text","text":"your current income precisely equals the value you currently create in the market.","bold":true}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"This means: you cannot say \"I am undervalued\"—if you were truly worth that much, you would have already received it. Complaining about the environment, your boss, or timing is just "},{"type":"text","text":"handing over decision-making power to others","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":". The author's stance is quite firm: as long as you allow others to decide your income, you also hand over the power to control your own life."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Accepting this premise is the starting point for all action advice in this chapter."}]},{"type":"h3","children":[{"type":"text","text":"2. What Constitutes Income? A Formula"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"The author breaks down \"income\" into five independently trainable components and provides a calculation formula:"}]},{"type":"blockquote","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Income = (Ability × Energy × Influence × Self-Esteem × Creativity) ÷ 2","bold":true}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Among these, Ability, Energy, Self-Esteem, and Creativity are each scored out of 10, while "},{"type":"text","text":"Influence is scored out of 100","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":"—it has 10 times the weight of all other components."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"For example, if you scored 5, 10, 3, 6, 6 respectively for the five items, your monthly income would be approximately 2700 euros. But if you simply increased Influence from 3 to 30, your monthly income would become 27000 euros—everything else remaining unchanged."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"The most important insight from this formula is: hard work (Ability, Energy) is a necessary condition, but by no means a decisive factor. The real leverage lies in how many people know you.","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":" This explains why two people with similar abilities can have incomes that differ by 10 times—some tennis stars can earn big money, not just because they play tennis well, but because thousands of people are watching them play."}]},{"type":"blockquote","children":[{"type":"text","text":"💡 "},{"type":"text","text":"This formula's applicability extends far beyond the workplace. Investing improves the \"Ability\" component, but its ceiling is obvious when capital is limited; side hustles/personal projects are the true path to leveraging the 100-point \"Influence\" variable—two developers with similar abilities, whose incomes differ by 10 times, the gap is almost always here.","italic":true}]},{"type":"h3","children":[{"type":"text","text":"3. How to Improve These Five Areas"}]},{"type":"h4","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Influence (Most Important)"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Doing what everyone else can do makes your value like a grain of sand in the desert. You cannot stand out by being \"better,\" because there are plenty of people who think they are better than others. "},{"type":"text","text":"The key is not to be better, but to be more unique.","bold":true}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"This means you need to make yourself an "},{"type":"text","text":"expert","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":" in a specific niche. Once you become an expert, you can limit your target audience to a \"small group,\" thereby setting higher prices."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"The path to becoming an expert is more concrete than most people imagine:"}]},{"type":"ol","children":[{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Identify your passion and talent, and determine which field you can dominate in 3 years."}]}]},{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"All decisions revolve around this goal, not around existing clients."}]}]},{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"There's an acceleration method: "},{"type":"text","text":"Write a full-page advertisement positioning yourself as an expert today (even if it's just a draft).","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":" This exercise will force you to examine your value from a client's perspective and immediately reveal what you are still lacking."}]}]}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Additionally, increasing influence also includes: publishing articles, public speaking, PR exposure, hosting events, building alliances with people in other fields for cross-promotion... "},{"type":"text","text":"Those who are not afraid of making mistakes pursue excellence; those who are afraid of making mistakes pursue perfection and achieve nothing.","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":" If 51% of quick decisions are right, that's enough to get rich."}]},{"type":"blockquote","children":[{"type":"text","text":"💡 "},{"type":"text","text":"This point is more critical in the context of side hustles/personal projects than in the workplace. Special Traps for Self-Employed Individuals"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"This section is essentially about "},{"type":"text","text":"using systems to protect yourself from human errors.","bold":true}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"A typical case for self-employed individuals: income fluctuates, they splurge during peak seasons and borrow during off-seasons, ending up in debt after a few years, yet never understanding where the money went. The solution is very simple: "},{"type":"text","text":"pay yourself a fixed \"salary\" each month based on the minimum expected income, strictly separate personal and business accounts, and the remaining money belongs to the company.","bold":true}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Another common trap is investing all money back into the company, completely betting personal wealth on the future sale price of the company. (Other People's Money, i.e., loans)—"},{"type":"text","text":"consumer debt should be strictly avoided, but business expansion can use leverage","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":", because effective business investments will increase turnover, and inflation will reduce the real value of loans."}]},{"type":"h3","children":[{"type":"text","text":"6. A Cognitive Boundary"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"An important conceptual distinction: "},{"type":"text","text":"high income ≠ wealth","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":"."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Standard of living automatically inflates to your income level. No matter how much you earn, \"necessary expenses\" will always fill the account."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"True wealth has only one definition: "},{"type":"text","text":"being able to live off the interest of your assets without needing to work.","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":" Achieving this goal is not about how much you earn, but how much you save—do you want to own a money-making machine, or forever be a money-making machine?"}]},{"type":"blockquote","children":[{"type":"text","text":"💡 "},{"type":"text","text":"This is also why simply increasing income is not enough: if living expenses inflate with income, net worth won't truly grow. Increasing income and controlling the savings rate must be pursued simultaneously.","italic":true}]},{"type":"h3","children":[{"type":"text","text":"🤔 Personal Interpretation: What This Chapter Means for My Current Situation"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"This chapter dedicates a lot of space to \"how to create more value and negotiate raises in the workplace,\" which has limited appeal for those who no longer rely on salary increases to accumulate wealth. However, if we strip the framework of this chapter from the \"workplace\" context and look at it independently, it remains highly relevant—because its underlying logic is not \"how to get your employer to pay you more,\" but "},{"type":"text","text":"\"where does income come from, and how to amplify it.\"","bold":true}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"The income formula is the most valuable takeaway.","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":" Apply it to areas beyond salary:"}]},{"type":"ul","children":[{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"The "},{"type":"text","text":"investment","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":" path is essentially about improving the \"ability\" component (financial judgment, ability to select targets). This is necessary, but it's one of the smallest multipliers in the formula. A more critical constraint is that the \"influence\" of investment is equivalent to the size of the principal—when the principal is small, even with high returns, the absolute profit is limited. This is not a reason to give up investing, but rather to say: before capital accumulates to a certain scale, relying solely on investment returns to \"get rich\" is very slow. The book places increasing income before saving/investing, and the logic is here."}]}]},{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"The "},{"type":"text","text":"side hustle","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":" path is where the formula truly has explosive potential. If a personal project gains users, if technical content builds a readership, if a certain reputation is established in a community—these all add to influence, and an increase in influence can amplify the value of all other efforts tenfold. This is why two developers with similar skill levels can have vastly different incomes."}]}]}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"So, the most useful question from this chapter for the present moment is: "},{"type":"text","text":"Which component am I investing my time in right now? Chapters 9 and 10 contain some independent content worth noting separately."}]},{"type":"h3","children":[{"type":"text","text":"1. The Goose Analogy: The Essence of Financial Freedom"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"These three chapters use the same imagery throughout: "},{"type":"text","text":"Goose = principal, Golden Egg = interest (passive income).","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":" The farmer killed the goose looking for gold, only to find nothing—most people's financial state is similar: spending all income, the principal never grows, and there are never any golden eggs."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Financial freedom has only one definition: "},{"type":"text","text":"the principal is large enough that its interest alone can cover living expenses.","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":" Before this, you work for money; after this, money works for you. The entire logic of saving and investing is preparing for this day."}]},{"type":"h3","children":[{"type":"text","text":"2. Savings: How to Keep Your Money"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Core Operation: Pay Yourself 10% at the Beginning of the Month","bold":true}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"On payday, immediately transfer 10% of your net income to a separate \"goose account\"; the remaining 90% is your usable income. Don't save what's left at the end of the month—this is where most savings plans fail."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"When You Get a Raise: Add 50% of the Raise to Your Goose Account","bold":true}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Since you haven't adapted to the higher standard of living after the raise, this 50% will barely be felt. This mechanism automatically increases your savings rate with your income, without needing to \"make a decision\" each time."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Strict Boundaries of the Goose Account:","bold":true}]},{"type":"ul","children":[{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Life insurance, pension insurance are not included in the 10%—those are other types of fixed expenses."}]}]},{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Money saved for short-term goals like travel or a new car is also not included—that's consumption savings."}]}]},{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Money in the goose account can only be invested for growth, never for consumption of the principal."}]}]}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"A counter-intuitive conclusion worth remembering: "},{"type":"text","text":"the lower the income, the easier it is to implement the savings percentage.","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":" Saving 10% of 1000 euros is 100 euros; saving 10% of 10000 euros is 1000 euros—the absolute amount is larger, and the psychological resistance is greater. \"I'll save when my income is higher\" is a self-fulfilling procrastination."}]},{"type":"h3","children":[{"type":"text","text":"3. Compound Interest: The Multiplier Effect of Time"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Only three variables affect the result of compound interest: "},{"type":"text","text":"time, profit rate, and principal.","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":" But the relationship between these three is multiplication, not addition—a small change in any one variable will lead to an order-of-magnitude difference."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"The impact of profit rate far exceeds intuition:","bold":true}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"With Rate"}]}]},{"type":"td","children":[{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Final 7,600 euros"}]}]}]},{"type":"tr","children":[{"type":"td","children":[{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"12%"}]}]},{"type":"td","children":[{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Approx. 30,000 euros"}]}]}]},{"type":"tr","children":[{"type":"td","children":[{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"20%"}]}]},{"type":"td","children":[{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Approx. 237,000 euros"}]}]}]}],"props":{"align":[]}},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Increasing the profit rate by 3 times does not result in 3 times the amount, but nearly 30 times."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"A Quick Mental Math Tool: The Rule of 72","bold":true}]},{"type":"blockquote","children":[{"type":"text","text":"72 ÷ Annual Interest Rate = This is why pursuing higher investment returns is worth spending time learning—even improving by a few percentage points has a huge long-term compounding effect."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"The role of time is equally irreplaceable:","bold":true}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Starting at age 30, saving 200 euros per month (12% annual return), by age 65 you would have approximately "},{"type":"text","text":"1.05 million euros","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":". Making Compound Interest a Muscle Memory"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"In addition to the mathematical principles of compound interest, Chapter 9 also proposes a specific behavioral exercise: "},{"type":"text","text":"start by saving 5 euro cents in the first month, double it each month, and persist for 18 months.","bold":true}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"5 euro cents → 10 euro cents → 20 euro cents... by the 16th month, you would need to save approximately 1600 euros, and by the 18th month, the cumulative total would exceed 13000 euros."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"The practical significance of this exercise is not in the small interest, but in two things: first, it psychologically forces you to "},{"type":"text","text":"find new sources of income","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":" in the first 14 months to cover the increasing deposit amount; second, it makes \"opening up income channels\" a habit, rather than a one-time decision. The author says it's \"exercising your income ability like exercising a muscle.\""}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Furthermore, Chapter 9 also points out the underlying logic of capitalism: the word capitalism itself contains \"capital.\" If you don't make capital and investment work for you, the entire capitalist system will quietly pass you by—economically, you are living in the financial Stone Age. Investors in Walmart in 1975 saw 90,000 euros turn into 26 million euros 20 years later, not by luck, but by letting compound interest run continuously without interruption."}]},{"type":"h3","children":[{"type":"text","text":"5. Why \"Later\" is the Most Dangerous Excuse"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"The core of Chapter 10 is a grim reality check: "},{"type":"text","text":"you can no longer rely on the state pension system.","bold":true}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"The author uses the story of Joseph interpreting Pharaoh's dream as an analogy: seven years of plenty are inevitably followed by seven years of famine. Most people live as if the famine will never come—they don't save enough during the years of plenty. And today's pension system, due to declining birth rates and an aging population, the intergenerational contract can no longer function normally; this is not a pessimistic prediction, but simple demographic mathematics."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"A more realistic problem is that the \"famine\" often begins before retirement—layoffs, industry decline, health problems—and those without sufficient reserves have no buffer against these shocks."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Another point worth noting from Chapter 10 is about "},{"type":"text","text":"excuses","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":": excuses are lies we tell ourselves. Each of us has two voices inside—the voice of financial failure and the voice of financial success. Whether we achieve financial freedom depends on which one we listen to more often. \"I'm not ready yet,\" \"I'll wait until the conditions are right\"—these words sound cautious, but in reality, they are seeking legitimacy for inaction."}]},{"type":"h3","children":[{"type":"text","text":"🤔 Personal Interpretation"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Saving itself isn't my problem; in fact, the opposite is true—spending too little is also a form of imbalance. But these three chapters contain a detail worth serious consideration:"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"The definition of a goose account is much stricter than \"having a lot of money.\"","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":" Money in a checking account, even if substantial, is not a \"goose\" if it hasn't been allocated to generate cash flow; it's just a pile of money waiting to be spent."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"So the real question to ask yourself is: "},{"type":"text","text":"How much of the money in my account is truly a \"golden egg-laying goose,\" and how much is just money that hasn't been spent yet?","bold":true}]},{"type":"hr","children":[{"type":"text","text":""}]},{"type":"h2","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Chapter 11 Principles for Investors and Stock Traders"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"This chapter is the core of the book's investment section, divided into two parts: "},{"type":"text","text":"seven investment principles","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":" and "},{"type":"text","text":"five important decisions that must be made","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":". The author explicitly states that this chapter does not provide specific investment advice, but only discusses underlying principles—because specific products change rapidly, but principles are enduring."}]},{"type":"h3","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Part One: Seven Investment Principles"}]},{"type":"h4","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Principle One: Distinguish Between Investing, Speculation, and Saving"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"There is only one criterion:","bold":true}]},{"type":"blockquote","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Money regularly flows into your pocket from the moment of purchase → Investing. Profit only comes from resale → Speculation. Money sits in a savings account untouched → Saving.","bold":true}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Specifically:"}]},{"type":"ul","children":[{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Saver","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":": Money goes into an account, no next step. Better than not saving, but money won't significantly appreciate."}]}]},{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Speculator","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":": Expects to profit from price fluctuations (buy low, sell high). Returns are unstable, no guaranteed regular cash flow. Speculation itself isn't bad—what's bad is "},{"type":"text","text":"thinking you're investing when you're actually The bank saying \"buying a house is an investment\" is correct—for the bank, your monthly interest payments are its income."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"This leads to an important order principle: "},{"type":"text","text":"Invest first, then incur debt (buy a house).","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":" If you buy a house first, you might never have spare money to invest; if you invest first, the returns from investing can help you buy a house more easily. Many families fail to accumulate wealth, not because of low income, but because the order is wrong."}]},{"type":"h4","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Principle Three: Three Asset Types"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"There are only three main categories of financial investment:"}]},{"type":"ol","children":[{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Monetary assets","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":": Savings, bonds, money market funds, etc. High security, but inflation erodes returns. If inflation is 4% and interest is 2%, you lose 2% annually in real terms. By the Rule of 72, at 4% inflation, your monetary purchasing power halves every 18 years."}]}]},{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Tangible assets: Inflation causes prices to rise, and tangible assets rise with them."}]}]}]},{"type":"blockquote","children":[{"type":"text","text":"72 ÷ Inflation Rate = Years for Monetary Purchasing Power to Halve","bold":true}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"This is also why, in the long run, putting all your money in a savings account is a decision that leads to chronic loss."}]},{"type":"h4","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Principle Five: You Must Take Risks"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Financial freedom and absolute safety are two opposing paths that cannot be walked simultaneously.","bold":true}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"People who seek safety prioritize \"not losing money,\" and their fear of loss outweighs their desire for profit. The result is: their money, while not \"lost,\" is slowly eroded by inflation and taxes, and after many years, the wealth they can command is far less than that of investors willing to take risks."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"People who seek freedom prioritize \"making money.\" This comes at a cost: courage, perseverance, being ready to make mistakes, and enduring occasional losses."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"An important point from the author: "},{"type":"text","text":"True investors view losses as part of profits.","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":" No wealthy investor has not experienced losses; but he knows many poor people who have never lost money in investments—because they have never truly invested."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Trying to completely avoid risk will paradoxically lead to losing more—because inflation is silently taxing you, and you're doing nothing."}]},{"type":"h4","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Principle Six: Diversification (Crucial)"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"No one can predict the future—whether it will be inflation or deflation, prosperity or recession. Profits in bull markets, only waits in bear markets. The advantage is that it requires almost no time. Historical data shows that long-term holding of stock funds averages over 12% annually—this slow path is viable, but takes about 20 years."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Investor","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":": Not satisfied with average returns, actively takes action even in bear markets. The cost is a lot of time and continuous learning, and making more mistakes, but viewing each mistake as part of success."}]},{"type":"h3","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Part Two: Five Important Decisions"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Principles are universal, but decisions are personal. Coaches and Expert Networks"}]},{"type":"h4","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Core Argument: Environment is More Reliable Than Willpower"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"The author uses a physics analogy to illustrate the point: you stand on a table, trying to pull someone standing on the ground up, while they only need to \"stay still\" to pull you down—because pulling down is much easier than pulling up."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"The meaning of this analogy is: "},{"type":"text","text":"relying on willpower to fight against your surroundings is destined to fail in the long run.","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":" The truly effective approach is not to become \"stronger,\" but to change your environment—to let the environment itself become the force that propels you forward."}]},{"type":"blockquote","children":[{"type":"text","text":"If you are surrounded by people poorer than you, you will stagnate. If you are surrounded by people richer than you, you will also become rich."}]},{"type":"h4","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Three Types of People Form an Ideal Environment"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"1. Coach/Mentor","bold":true}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"\"Coach\" here does not refer to a sports coach, nor specifically an investor, but rather "},{"type":"text","text":"someone who has achieved far greater success than you in the field you aspire to, and is willing to guide your growth","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":"—this could be an entrepreneur, a successful person in a certain industry, or any master in a field you wish to learn."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"The essence of this relationship is closer to a hybrid of \"mentor + partner\": the book suggests giving a portion of company equity to the coach, with the logic that \"50% of 10 million euros is far better than 100% of 50,000 euros.\" By giving up a portion of the profits, you gain the coach's genuine investment of time and resources—forming a true alignment of interests, rather than a one-sided guidance relationship."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"99% of outstanding successful people have coaches. Learning from a truly successful person for 6 months is better than fumbling on your own for 10 years."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"The key to finding a mentor is not luck, but "},{"type":"text","text":"what value you can offer the other person","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":"—a mentor won't spend time on you for no reason; you need to provide a reason for their investment. The author provides 17 tips for interacting with mentors, the core principles of which can be condensed into a few points:"}]},{"type":"ul","children":[{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Understand why you need a mentor and what you can do for them."}]}]},{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Approach them with passion and specific goals, rather than vaguely \"seeking guidance.\""}]}]},{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Respect the mentor's time; be fully prepared for every conversation."}]}]},{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Don't push problems onto the mentor to solve; instead, bring 3 alternative solutions and ask which one is best."}]}]},{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Accept tests—truly excellent mentors often test your endurance and determination first."}]}]},{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Repay the mentor through your success, not just verbal thanks."}]}]}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"2. Role Models","bold":true}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Identify the best people in your field and study their mindset, work habits, values, and money views. This \"imitation of excellence\" is not about blindly copying behaviors, but about deeply observing and understanding the inner logic of successful people, gradually enabling yourself to think and perceive in the same way."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"3. Expert Network","bold":true}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Actively meet one person each month who is more successful than you in a certain field, and maintain these relationships long-term. There is only one key mindset for building an expert network: "},{"type":"text","text":"first think about what you can offer the other person, not what you can get from them.","bold":true}]},{"type":"h4","children":[{"type":"text","text":"A Position That Needs Clarification"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"The author says \"never be influenced by those less successful than you,\" which sounds extreme. He adds an explanation: helping others and learning from successful people are not contradictory, just as day and night together form a complete nature. The more successful you are in managing your own life, the wider your ability to help others—but when helping others, do not, in turn, follow their advice."}]},{"type":"h3","children":[{"type":"text","text":"2. Sowing Money"}]},{"type":"h4","children":[{"type":"text","text":"A Counter-Intuitive Phenomenon"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"The author observes a pattern that cannot be fully explained by logic: "},{"type":"text","text":"those who regularly donate 10% of their income often become richer than those who keep 100% of their income.","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":" How can 90% be more than 100%?"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"He doesn't claim this has scientific basis, but offers several possible explanations:"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Giving changes your relationship with money.","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":" When you are able to give, you are proving to yourself that you have more than you need. This \"sense of abundance\" influences how you treat money, making you less clingy, and instead more naturally attracting more money."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Giving proves money is a good thing.","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":" Many people have an implicit guilt about money, feeling that being rich is selfish. When you use money to do good, you confirm deep down that \"money is a tool that can be used for good\"—this belief itself can change how you accumulate and use money."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Giving brings vitality and a sense of meaning.","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":" People who only focus on themselves become lonely and depressed. Giving makes one feel connected to others, and this sense of fulfillment, in turn, boosts motivation."}]},{"type":"h4","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Practical Application"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"It is recommended to consistently donate 1/10 of your income to others, and "},{"type":"text","text":"not to wait until you \"have enough money\" to start.","bold":true}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Historically, famous wealthy individuals—Carnegie, Rockefeller, Templeton—all began donating when they had almost nothing. The author believes that it was this expectation of abundance, rather than waiting for abundance to arrive before giving, that contributed to their later success."}]},{"type":"h3","children":[{"type":"text","text":"3. Knowledge is Power Only When Applied"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"There's a sentence in the book worth remembering as a summary of the entire work:"}]},{"type":"blockquote","children":[{"type":"text","text":"The adage \"knowledge is power\" is actually incorrect. The correct statement should be: knowledge is power only when applied.","bold":true}]},{"type":"h3","children":[{"type":"text","text":"🤔 Personal Interpretation"}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"The most resonant part of Chapter 13 for me is the underlying logic that \"environment is more reliable than willpower.\" Fighting against an environment that drags you down with self-discipline is a battle destined to be exhausting. The smarter approach is to actively choose and build your environment—this is the same idea as \"actively choosing the people around you\" in Chapter 7, just explained more systematically in this chapter."}]},{"type":"p","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Chapter 14, taken alone, might seem a bit mystical, but when viewed in the context of the entire book's logic, it's actually talking about something very practical: your attitude towards money determines what you can do. A person who feels \"money is not enough\" and a person who feels \"I have enough money to give\" have completely different action patterns. Donating 10% is not just helping others, but also actively shaping your own money beliefs—and beliefs, as this book has emphasized from Chapter 1, are fundamental."}]}]},"reading":null}]},{"_sys":{"filename":"index","basename":"index.mdx","hasReferences":null,"breadcrumbs":["en","a-dog-called-money","index"],"path":"content/notes/en/a-dog-called-money/index.mdx","relativePath":"en/a-dog-called-money/index.mdx","extension":".mdx"},"id":"content/notes/en/a-dog-called-money/index.mdx","__typename":"NoteSeries","createdAt":"2026-02-08T06:50:19.761Z","updatedAt":"2026-02-09T13:57:35.142Z","canonicalId":"a-dog-called-money","seriesName":"A Don't \"kill the goose\" for immediate consumption; let the principal appreciate continuously through compound interest."}]}]},{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"When interest income (golden eggs) can support living expenses, financial freedom is achieved."}]}]}]}]},{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Principles of Fund Investment","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":":"}]},{"type":"ul","children":[{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Choose equity funds that are "},{"type":"text","text":"at least 10 years old","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":" and "},{"type":"text","text":"large multinational","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":"."}]}]},{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Long-term holding","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":": Be prepared for a 5-10 year investment cycle, and do not sell due to short-term market downturns."}]}]}]}]},{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Financial Calculation Tools","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":":"}]},{"type":"ul","children":[{"type":"li","children":[{"type":"lic","children":[{"type":"text","text":"Rule of 72","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":": Use \"72 divided by the annualized interest rate\" to get the "},{"type":"text","text":"time required for the principal to double","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":"; you can also use \"72 divided by the inflation rate\" to get the "},{"type":"text","text":"time for money to halve in value","bold":true},{"type":"text","text":"."}]}]}]}]}]},{"type":"h3","children":[{"type":"text","text":"V.
